B. Pre-Application Discussion for a Proposed Amendment to the Planned Development
   of Crossroads Shopping Center at 113-229 Skokie Valley Rd. to: Modify the Parking
   and Site Plan; Construct a 1400 Sq. Ft. Building Addition; and, Grant an Exception
   to Section 150.408 to Allow the Use of Sale of Soft Drinks by Vending Machine
   Outside of a Building.

   Planner Cross made a presentation for the above item including: application summary,
   site plan modifications, building addition, outdoor sales, issues for consideration, parking
   and refuse, police and fire department concerns and recommendations.

   Mr. Steve Goodman, Meltzer, Purtill & Stelle, 300 S. Wacker Dr., Chicago, IL 60606,
   attorney for the applicant, stated he would take questions from the Commission.

   Commissioner Reinstein asked about the outdoor sales and the time limitations.

   Manager Sloan stated outdoor sales were allowed as an accessory use for 180 days per
   year and this time could be extended by the City Manager's office. The issue with the
   machines is that they are not associated with, as an accessory use, to any of the principal
   uses presently in the center. The center wants to do it on its own in a common area but
   does not possess a separate principal use.

   Commissioner Reinstein asked if the sales area it would be limited to pop machines.

   Manager Sloan stated the proposal is for pop machines only.

   Commissioner Reinstein asked where the locations were.

   Mr. Goodman stated one of them would be located on the north side of Party City and the
   other location is near LA Fitness.

   Commissioner Reinstein asked if these would be there during the temperate months.

   Mr. Goodman stated they would be there all winter.

   Manager Sloan stated it would be on a permanent basis.

   Commissioner Reinstein asked if it would be just these machines on a permanent basis.
   He asked if someone else wanted to install some machines would they have to go through
   the normal process.

                           Regular Meeting of the Plan Commission
                                 Tuesday, November 5, 2013
                                           2 of 8
Manager Sloan stated if one of the principal uses wanted to put something outside they
would apply for a permit.

Commissioner Reinstein asked if this would cover anything else.

Manager Sloan stated no.

Commissioner Reinstein asked what the distance was between the SW corner of new 1400
s.f. space and the curve of the drive. He asked if there would be an entry/exit point from
the retail space in this location.

Mr. Goodman they were in the preliminary planning stages and did not know.

Commissioner Reinstein asked if there were ongoing negotiations with the user.

Mr. Goodman stated there are ongoing discussions, and, that due to the existing tenancies
of the spaces that the tenant would occupy, they did not want to get too far ahead with
details and elevations. He estimated that construction would probably not start until 2015.

Commissioner Bilotti asked if the space was 27,000 sf., with an additional 7,000 sf. of
restaurant space or 7000 sf. within the grocery space, because he did not see it depicted on
the plan.

Mr. Goodman stated it is not depicted on the plan. They are saying in lieu of 7,000 s.f. of
retail, they are looking for the flexibility of adding up to an additional 7,000 s.f. of
restaurant space. There is nothing concrete at this time.

Commissioner Bilotti asked about the extension toward the street. He asked if the present
outdoor seating and bike racks would be removed.

Mr. Goodman stated the intention is to relocate as much as possible. The outdoor seating
is popular and they agree with the comments in the staff report regarding the need to
provide a buffer between the street and the outdoor seating. The seating area may be
reduced in size, but the intention is to keep it.

Commissioner Bilotti stated he hoped they would keep the bike racks.

Commissioner Kaplan stated there seemed to be enough parking on the north and south
side of the center. He asked that if a grocery store would occupy, would the north side
spaces be utilized. He stated it was important to know where the restaurant parking would
be located. He asked on which side of the building would be the entry for the grocery and
its parking.

Mr. Goodman replied this had not been determined.

Commissioner Kaplan stated in terms of parking concerns the location of the door might
soften concerns about parking and pedestrian conflicts. He stated the vending machines
were not uncommon and asked who would receive the income from the machines.

                        Regular Meeting of the Plan Commission
                              Tuesday, November 5, 2013
                                        3 of 8
Manager Sloan stated she thought they would belong to Federal Realty.

Commissioner Kaplan stated with Binny's and the fitness center, he questioned the
sensibility and aesthetic appeal of having free standing vending machines. He stated he
was not particularly in favor of these, but did not think it was a huge issue.

Mr. Brian Donley, Federal Realty, 50 E. Wynnewood Rd., Wynnewood, PA, the
applicant, stated the vending machines are a national deal between Federal Realty and
Coke. These are located in shopping centers all over the country.

Commissioner Kaplan asked if there was any sales tax implication.

Manager Sloan stated the applicant could supply this information. She stated the use of
the entire center is related to the ability to meet parking demand. At the next meeting part
of the discussion would be about the total amount of parking and amount of parking
demand.

Commissioner Glenner stated the applicant may come back and advise the impact of the
grocery store and also the positive impacts for strengthening the other tenants in the area
by the presence of the grocery store.

Manager Sloan stated grocery stores have taxable and non-taxable items but she was not
sure about the sales tax net change, but that this is something that could also be supplied at
public hearing..

Commissioner Glazer mentioned the number of spaces and that the drive aisles were
narrower than required by code. He asked if the police had concerns regarding this.

Manager Sloan stated they would review this and they were mostly concerned about the
fire lane access.

Commissioner Glazer asked if this would require relief.

Manager Sloan stated the point of a PUD is to be flexible and allow relief. If aisles are
less than required it would need relief.

Planner Cross stated the previous drive aisles were one-way each way and they have
reconfigured it to have two-way traffic and 90 stalls. The fire and police departments
have not had the opportunity to review the site plan. The deficiency is 3". He stated the
Commission has the authority to recommend a grant of relief to these specifications.
Copies of the new plans will be sent to the police and fire departments.

Mr. Dan Brinkman, Gewalt Hamilton Associates, 850 Forest Edge Dr., Vernon Hills, IL,
traffic consultant, stated the dimensions on the 90 aisle are 25'-5" and the city ordinance
states 25'-8". He did not think this would be a problem.

Commissioner Glazer asked about the restaurant and where it would be located.



                        Regular Meeting of the Plan Commission
                              Tuesday, November 5, 2013
                                        4 of 8
Mr. Goodman replied it was conceptual in nature at this time and could be in any number
of spaces in the center as tenant leases expire.

Commissioner Glazer asked if it would be adjacent to the grocery.

Mr. Goodman replied it could be but at present it is not intended to be.

Commissioner Bilotti stated there is some vacancy there now.

Manager Sloan stated the Applicant is trying to allocate the parking so they have the
flexibility to go from a retail tenant to a restaurant tenant in the future. The parking
calculations are currently based on the existing configuration in the center which has two
restaurants. Restaurants have a higher parking requirement than retail.

Mr. Donley stated the most likely space for a restaurant is between the new space and
Binny's.

Commissioner Glazer asked about the possible need for enhanced sanitation services.

Mr. Goodman stated the applicant has an existing refuse removal program and the new
tenant would adhere to that program. Some groceries have their own removal program
and they would consider their program.

Commissioner Glazer asked about compost and if this is something they would consider.

Mr. Goodman stated they would work with staff and consider what is proposed. It is
something the new tenant would need to be comfortable with if it made sense.

Commissioner Kaplan mentioned the bicycle parking and thought it would be helpful if
there were multiple bike parking locations dispersed throughout the development.

Mr. Goodman stated they could look into it.

Commissioner Reinstein asked if there is sufficient parking for peak and non-peak with
the new proposed uses.

Mr. Brinkman stated this was correct and they had looked at peak demands for the
existing center and calculated the peak demands for the proposed center.

Commissioner Reinstein asked if the City had in-house staff to review these studies.

Manager Sloan stated it does, but sometimes third party review is used and it is likely for
is applicaiton.

Commissioner Reinstein asked if this could be done now.

Manager Sloan stated they normally wait until they have the full application so they have
all the details.

                        Regular Meeting of the Plan Commission

Commissioner Glazer stated he thought this was a worthy project and they should look at
the parking study to see if the City agrees with the study or if a closer look is necessary.

Commissioner Bilotti asked if the land bank is sufficient to cover the additional parking
demands and if they need a parking study.

Manager Sloan stated the land bank is unbuilt. They may submit the application with the
intent to build out the land bank or not.

Commissioner Bilotti asked how many spaces there were in the land bank.

Manager Sloan stated there were 41 spaces.

Commissioner Glenner stated the applicant is focused on parking. He wanted to hear
about the shared parking, employee parking, re-striping and easements to the south. He
appreciated the applicant's efforts.

Manager Sloan stated the center is subject to cross access agreements and some triggers
for evaluating the need for a signal at the center aisle as a result of when Thorntons was
established. She thought that these obligations were satisfied, but it is possible that this
issue may need to be revisited with the new uses in the center.

Commissioner Glenner asked about the grocery and if they had been identified.

Ms. Sloan stated that the grocery tenant has asked for confidentiality at this time.

Councilman Blumberg mentioned the notice, distance requirements, and who needed to be
notified.

Manager Sloan stated all owners within 400' had to be notified.

Councilman Blumberg asked about current policy considerations regarding outdoor
vending machines.

Manager Sloan stated the code allows infinite extensions and cited Red Box at Walgreens
as an example.

Councilman Blumberg asked what Red Boxes were.

Manager Sloan replied they were video rentals.

Councilman Blumberg asked if this was something that disturbed a portion of the
population.

Manager Sloan stated she did know that Vice Chair Stolberg is not in favor of vending
machines and thinks they attract problems, i.e., break-ins, litter, etc. One concern is
depending on which way the machines are oriented, they serve as illuminated signage like
billboards, or off-site signage, for which there are some sign code issues. There have been
some businesses that have never sought a permit for these machines.

Project
Description:                    Demolition of an existing gasoline station, attendant kiosk, and motor vehicle
                                washing facility and construction of a new gasoline station, convenience food
                                mart without outdoor patio, motor vehicle washing facility and outdoor sales
                                space

Process:                        Planned Development and Conditional Use Permit

PREVIOUS CONSIDERATION:

In December 2010, the applicant, Buchanan Energy Company, purchased 81 Exxon Mobil gasoline
stations in the Chicago market, including the existing one at 1333 Half Day Road. The current gasoline
station use is authorized and guided by a Special Use Permit that was granted in 1978 (Ordinance No. 30-
78). As a new owner, the applicant is seeking to invest in and improve the property through the voluntary
Planned Unit Development process. The improvements would consist of:

          1) the demolition of the existing structures, which include 5 fuel pumps, an attendant kiosk, and a
          motor vehicle washing facility; and,

          2) the construction of a new gasoline station with 8 "dive-in" style fuel pumps, a 4,706 sq. ft.
          convenience food mart and a 2,282 sq. ft. motor vehicle washing facility that can wash 3 cars at
          any given time.

On January 15, 2013, the Plan Commission conducted a Public Hearing (#12-06-PUD-002 and #12-06-
SUP-001) to consider the proposed Planned Development and Conditional Use for a gasoline station with
a convenience food mart and motor vehicle washing facility at the subject property. No members of the
public were present to comment on the proposal. The Plan Commission considered the proposal under the
standards in Articles V and XIV of the Zoning Code and voted (6-0) to direct staff to draft Findings of
Fact recommending City Council approval of the proposal on several conditions (outlined below).

City Council

The Plan Commission's recommended conditions were considered by the City Council on April 8, 2013,
at which point the Council directed Corporation Counsel to prepare the necessary approval documents.
On May 13, 2013, the City Council adopted a Resolution (#R66-13) to approve a Preliminary
Development Plan for the site on the following conditions:

         The applicant will provide the following public benefits in exchange for the requested relief: 1)
          the extension of the sidewalk on the subject property to connect the existing sidewalk to the
          northeastern corner of Skokie Valley Road and Half Day Road; and, 2) a signalized crosswalk to
          connect the north and south sides of Half Day Road east of Skokie Valley Road

         The applicant will be required to plant the required number of inches of trees required as a result
          of the tree removal at the subject property (or the payment of a fee-in-lieu) as determined by the
          City Forester

         Prior to approval of a Final Plan of Development, the applicant must secure a cross-access

         Prior to approval of a Final Plan of Development, the applicant must secure permission from the

          identify the appropriate locations on the subject property for the underground tank venting system
          stacks and the monument signage

         The petitioner shall meet all of the requirements of Article V of Chapter 150 of the Highland Park
          Municipal Code for the filing of a Final Plan of Development

         The motor vehicle washing facility will be closed during the hours of 11 p.m. and 5 a.m.

POLICY:

As noted, the applicant received approval of a Preliminary Planned Development and Commercial Use
pursuant to a Resolution adopted by the City Council on May 13, 2013. Section 150.535 of the Zoning
Code outlines the filing requirements for a Final Development Plan application, and requires the applicant
to initiate the "second stage" of the Planned Development process by submitting specific documents and
information for Plan Commission review within six months of approval by the City Council. The six
month deadline to submit the required documents for the application is November 13, 2013.

Section 150.535(C) of the Zoning Code affords applicants the ability to submit a written request for an
extension of this deadline, and notes that "the Plan Commission, for good cause, may extend the period
for filing the Final Development Plan for a period not to exceed an additional six months."Per the
attached letter submitted by the applicant, dated November 1, 2013, the applicant is requesting Plan
Commission consideration of a six month extension to file the Final Development Plan application
materials to enable the applicant to continue its negotiations for a cross-access easement with the
neighbor to the north and to address recent comments from the Illinois Department of Transportation
(IDOT).

If the Plan Commission grants the applicant's request for a six month extension, the applicant will be
required to submit all materials for Plan Commission consideration by May 13, 2014. In the instance that
the applicant does not file the Final Development Plan within the allotted extended time period, Section
150.535(D) notes the following:

          (D)      Failure to File. Upon the failure of the applicant to file a complete Final Development
          Plan, in accordance with this Section 150.535, within six months of approval by the City Council

11-19-13\final documents\buckys extension request staff report 11-19-13.docx
                      REQUEST FOR PLAN COMMISSION ACTION

          of the preliminary Development Plan, or within the extended period approved by the Plan
          Commission pursuant to Section 150.535(C) of this Article, the Preliminary Development Plan
          approval by the City Council shall be considered null and void and of no force or effect.

RECOMMENDATION:

The Department of Community Development recommends that the Plan Commission consider the
applicant's request for a time extension to submit the Final Development Plan. If the Commission finds
that an extension for the filing should be granted, it is recommended that the Plan Commission should
move to extend the deadline for submittal for a period of six months, in accordance with Section
150.535(C) of the Zoning Code.

Dear Ms. Cates:

On May 13, 2013, the City Council adopted a Resolution approving a
Preliminary Planned Unit Development for the reconstruction of the
referenced facility. The Zoning Ordinance requires that the applicant file an
application for a Final Development Plan within six (6) months of that date.

As the staff is aware, we have been negotiating the extension of our cross
access agreement with the owner of the adjoining property to our west.
We have recently been informed that IDOT has requested them to close the
driveway that serves the cross access. We are working with IDOT and our
neighbor to arrive at a mutually agreeable solution, however, at this time
that is not finalized.

On behalf of our client, Buchanan Energy, LLC, we hereby request a six
month extension to file our Final Development Plan, as allowed by Section
150.535(A) of the Zoning Code.

We will continue to keep the City updated on our progress.


Sincerely,

                                         CITY OF HIGHLAND PARK
                                          RESOLUTION NO. R66-13
                A RESOLUTION APPROVING A PRELIMINARY DEVELOPMENT PLAN
                                   (1333 Half Day Road)

       WHEREAS, Buchanan Energy (N), LLC ("Applicant") is the record owner of that certain parcel of real
property consisting of approximately 1.26 acres, located in the B3 Highway Commercial District of the City ("B3
District"), commonly known as 1333 Half Day Road, Highland Park, Illinois, and legally described in Exhibit A
attached to and, by this reference, made a part of this Resolution ("Property"); and

       WHEREAS, the Property is currently improved with a gas station equipped with five fuel pumps, an
attendant kiosk, and a car wash ("Existing Development"); and

       WHEREAS, the Applicant desires to demolish the Existing Development on the Property, and to
construct a gas station equipped with eight fuel pumps, a convenience store, a car wash ("Car Wash"), and
outdoor space to be used for the sale of goods on the Property (collectively, the "Proposed Development"); and

        WHEREAS, the Proposed Development contemplates work by the Applicant in rights-of-way under the
jurisdiction of the Illinois Department of Transportation ("IDOT"); and

       WHEREAS, pursuant to Section 150.505(E) of the "City of Highland Park Zoning Ordinance of 1997," as
amended ("Zoning Code"), the Applicant has voluntarily elected to seek approval of a special use permit for a
planned development in order to construct the Proposed Development; and

        WHEREAS, pursuant to Article V of the Zoning Code, the Applicant has filed an application with the
City for approval of: (i) a planned development for the Property; and (ii) certain zoning modifications within the
planned development; and

        WHEREAS, a public hearing of the Plan Commission of the City of Highland Park to consider approval
of a planned development for the Property was duly advertised on December 24, 2012 in the Lake County News-
Sun, opened on January 15, 2013, and concluded on February 5, 2013; and

       WHEREAS, on February 5, 2013, the Plan Commission adopted Findings of Fact, Public Hearing Nos.
#12-06-PUD-002 and #12-06-SUP-001, recommending to the City Council preliminary approval of the planned
development for the Property; and

        WHEREAS, the City Council has determined that it will serve and be in the best interest of the City
and its residents to approve the preliminary development plan for the Property;

    NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED BY THE CITY COUNCIL OF HIGHLAND PARK, LAKE
COUNTY, ILLINOIS, as follows:

        SECTION ONE:             RECITALS. The foregoing recitals are incorporated into, and made a part of,
this Resolution as findings of the City Council.

         SECTION TWO:         APPROVAL OF PRELIMINARY DEVELOPMENT PLAN. The preliminary
development plan for the proposed planned development on the Property, consisting of the following documents
(collectively, "Preliminary Development Plan"), shall be, and is hereby, approved:

               A.      The Site Plan, consisting of 1 sheet and prepared by ARC Design Resources, Inc., with a
               latest revision date of March 7, 2013, a copy of which is attached to and, by this reference, made
               a part of this Resolution as Exhibit B;
              B.      The Landscape Plan, consisting of 1 sheet and prepared by ARC Design Resources, Inc.,
              with a latest revision date of March 7, 2013, a copy of which is attached to and, by this reference,
              made a part of this Resolution as Exhibit C;

              C.      The Tree Preservation Plan, consisting of 1 sheet and prepared by ARC Design
              Resources, Inc., with a latest revision date of August 13, 2012, a copy of which is attached to and,
              by this reference, made a part of this Resolution as Exhibit D;

              D.      The Aerial Exhibit, consisting of 1 sheet and prepared by ARC Design Resources, Inc.,
              with a latest revision date of April 27, 2012, a copy of which is attached to and, by this reference,
              made a part of this Resolution as Exhibit E;

              E.      The South Canopy Elevation, consisting of 1 sheet and prepared by Kurtz Associates
              Architects, as approved by the City Design Review Commission on March 4, 2013, a copy of
              which is attached to and, by this reference, made a part of this Resolution as Exhibit F;

              F.      The Exterior Building Elevations, consisting of 1 sheet and prepared by Robert W. Engel
              and Associates, with a latest revision date of November 2, 2012, a copy of which is attached to
              and, by this reference, made a part of this Resolution as Exhibit G;

              G.      The Front Elevation, consisting of 1 sheet and prepared by Bucky's, with a latest revision
              date of February 7, 2013, a copy of which is attached to and, by this reference, made a part of
              this Resolution as Exhibit H;

              H.      The Side Elevations, consisting of 1 sheet and prepared by Bucky's, with a latest revision
              date of February 7, 2013, a copy of which is attached to and, by this reference, made a part of
              this Resolution as Exhibit I;

              I.      The Back Elevation, consisting of 1 sheet and prepared by Bucky's, with a latest revision
              date of February 7, 2013, a copy of which is attached to and, by this reference, made a part of
              this Resolution as Exhibit J;

              J.      The Floor Plans and Notes, consisting of 1 sheet and prepared by Robert W. Engel and
              Associates, with a latest revision date of November 2, 2012, a copy of which is attached to and,
              by this reference, made a part of this Resolution as Exhibit K;

              K.     Those certain plans comprising the Sign Plan, consisting of 7 sheets and prepared by
              Omaha Neon Sign Co., Inc., with a latest revision date of March 12, 2013, copies of which are
              attached to and, by this reference, made a part of this Resolution as Group Exhibit L;

              L.      The Fuel Pump Designs, consisting of 2 sheets and prepared by LSI Graphic Solutions
              Plus, with a latest revision date of October 28, 2008, a copy of which is attached to and, by this
              reference, made a part of this Resolution as Exhibit M;

              M.      The Lighting Proposal, consisting of 1 sheet and prepared by LSI Industries, with a
              latest revision date of November 30, 2012, a copy of which is attached to and, by this reference,
              made a part of this Resolution as Exhibit N; and

              N.      The Site Utility Plan, consisting of 1 sheet and prepared by ARC Design Resources, Inc.,
              with a latest revision date of November 5, 2012, a copy of which is attached to and, by this
              reference, made a part of this Resolution as Exhibit O;

SECTION THREE: ACKNOWLEDGMENT OF REQUEST FOR CONDITIONAL USE PERMITS. The
City Council hereby acknowledges that the Applicant has requested, and that the proposed planned
development contemplates, issuance by the City of special use permits for a conditional use to permit the



                                                       2
operation of a gasoline and diesel fuel station and of a motor vehicle washing facility on the Property. At the
time of consideration of a final development plan for the planned development, the City Council shall consider
the requested special use permits in accordance with, and pursuant to, Section 150.411 and Article XIV of the
Zoning Code.

SECTION FOUR:          ACKNOWLEDGMENT OF REQUEST FOR ZONING MODIFICATIONS AND
CITY CODE RELIEF. Pursuant to Section 150.530(I)(1)(b) of the Zoning Code, the City Council hereby
acknowledges that the Applicant has requested, and that the proposed planned development contemplates, the
following modifications from the Zoning Code and the following relief from the City Code:

A.      A variation from Section 93.235(G) of "The Highland Park Code of 1968", as amended ("City Code"), to
increase the permitted width of the driveway located at the property line of the Property abutting Half Day
Road, from 30 feet to 52 feet;

B.      A modification from Section 150.408(B)(3) of the Zoning Code to permit utilization of the outdoor sales
area of the Proposed Development throughout each year;

C.      A modification from Section 150.707(A)(8) of the Zoning Code to permit the construction of an otherwise-
prohibited fence in a required front yard;

D.     A modification from Section 150.707(D)(1) of the Zoning Code to permit the otherwise-prohibited
construction of an accessory structure in a required front yard;

E.     A modification from Section 150.808(D)(6)(a) of the Zoning Code to decrease the number of required
stacking spaces at the entrance of the Car Wash, from 30 spaces to 11 spaces; and

F.     A modification from Section 150.707(H) to permit the installation of a monument sign within the
required sight triangle located on the Property at the intersection of the Route 41 and Half Day Road rights-of-
way ("Proposed Monument Sign").

At the time of consideration of a final development plan for the planned development, the City Council shall
consider the requested modifications and relief in accordance with, and pursuant to, Article V of the Zoning
Code.

       SECTION FIVE:           SUBMISSION OF FINAL DEVELOPMENT PLAN. Pursuant to and in
accordance with Section 150.535(A) of the Zoning Code, the adoption of this Resolution authorizes the Applicant
to submit a final development plan for the Property to the Plan Commission of the City.

SECTION SIX:            EFFECT OF APPROVALS. Pursuant to Section 150.530(I)(2) of the Zoning Code, the
approval of the Preliminary Development Plan for the Property, as set forth in Section Two of this Resolution,
shall not be deemed or interpreted as authorizing or entitling the development or the improvement of the
Property in any manner whatsoever unless and until the City Council approves, by ordinance or resolution duly
adopted, as the case may be, a special use permit for a planned development and a final development plan for
the Property, pursuant to Section 150.540(C) of the Zoning Code. Nothing herein shall be deemed or interpreted
as obligating or requiring the City Council to approve a special use permit or final development plan. Further,
the City Council shall have no obligation to consider or approve a special use permit for a planned development
or final development plan unless and until:

               A.     The Applicant complies with the applicable procedures for review and approval of a final
               development plan for the Property, as set forth in Sections 150.535 and 150.540 of the Zoning
               Code, which plan shall include, without limitation, a waste reduction and recycling plan for the
               Proposed Development, as required pursuant to Section 171.041 of the City Code;

               B.     The Applicant prepares and submits a final landscaping plan for the Property, for review
               and approval by the City Forester; and



                                                       3
            C.      The Applicant prepares and submits a stormwater drainage plan for the Property, for
            review and approval by the City Engineer, by which plan adequate stormwater detention volume
            shall be provided on the Property.

       SECTION SEVEN: CONDITIONS OF APPROVAL. Approval of a final development plan for the
Property shall be expressly conditioned upon the following:

            A.      Development Agreement. The Applicant shall enter into a development agreement with
            the City, to be prepared by the City's Corporation Counsel and subject to the approval of the City
            Council ("Development Agreement"), which Development Agreement shall govern and restrict
            the use and development of the Property, and shall contain, at a minimum and without
            limitation, the following provisions, conditions, and restrictions:

                   1.     The Applicant shall install a sidewalk on the north side of Half Day Road,
                   extending to the west from the existing sidewalk located on the north side of Half Day
                   Road to the intersection of Skokie Valley Road and Half Day Road ("Sidewalk");

                   2.      The Applicant shall install a signalized pedestrian crosswalk at the intersection
                   of Half Day Road and Skokie Valley Road, connecting the north and south sides of Half
                   Day Road along the east side of Skokie Valley Road ("Crosswalk");

                   3.      Prior to the issuance of any construction or demolition permit, the Applicant
                   shall cause to be fully executed, and shall comply with all terms and conditions of, a
                   cross-access agreement with the owner of the property located at 2635 Skokie Valley
                   Road for cross-access for the Property to allow for ingress to and egress from the
                   Property, as depicted in the Preliminary Development Plan ("Cross-Access Agreement");

                   4.       The Applicant shall install venting system stacks for underground tanks, in
                   specific locations that will minimize any adverse impact on nearby residential properties,
                   as mutually determined by the City and the Applicant;

                   5.      The Proposed Monument Sign shall be installed in a specific location that will
                   minimize visual obstructions to vehicles and pedestrians,        to minimize visual
                   obstructions for vehicles and pedestrians, as mutually determined by the City and the
                   Applicant;

                   6.      The Applicant shall not operate the Car Wash on the Property prior to 5:00 a.m.
                   and after 11:00 p.m. on any day;

                   7.      The Applicant shall cooperate in good faith with the City to monitor the adequacy
                   of stormwater detention volume on the Property and the release of stormwater from the
                   Property into the City storm sewer system, and shall comply with all applicable laws
                   relating to the improvement of stormwater detention volume on the Property and the
                   control of the release of stormwater into the City storm sewer system;

                   8.      The Applicant shall comply with the applicable tree replacement provisions set
                   forth in Chapter 94 of the City Code; and

                   9.      In addition to any other costs, payments, fees, charges, contributions, or
                   dedications required by the City's codes, ordinances, resolutions, rules, regulations, or by
                   the Development Agreement, the Applicant shall pay to the City, immediately upon
                   presentation a written demand or demands therefor, all legal, engineering, and other
                   consulting or administrative fees, costs, and expenses incurred or accrued in connection
                   with the review and processing of the plans for the Proposed Development and in




                                                    4
                       connection with the negotiation, preparation, consideration, and review of the
                       Development Agreement.

                B.       IDOT Approval for Work in the Rights-of-Way. Prior to the issuance of any construction
                or demolition permit, the Applicant shall obtain all necessary permits and approvals from IDOT
                for: (1) installation of the Sidewalk; (2) installation of the Crosswalk; and (3) any and all other
                work requiring permits and approvals from IDOT as set forth in the Preliminary Development
                Plan.

SECTION EIGH'[':        TIME PERIOD FOR SUBMISSION OF FINAL DEVELOPMENT PLAN. The final
development plan for the Property shall be submitted by the Applicant for review and approval by the City no
later than the date that is six months after the effective date of this Resolution, in accordance with and
pursuant to Section l.50.535(A) of the Zoning Code. Pursuant to Section 150.535(C) of the Zoning Code, upon
the written request of the Applicant, the Plan Commission, for good cause, may extend the period for filing the
final development plan for a period not to exceed an additional six months.

SECTION NINE: EFFECTIVE DATE. This Resolution shall be in full force and effect upon its passage and
approval by a majority of the members of the City Council.

AYES:                     Mayor Rotering, Councilmen Stone, Kaufman, Frank, Blumberg, Naftzger, and
                          Knobel

NAYS:                      None

ABSENT:                    None

PASSED:                    May 13, 2013

APPROVED:                  May 13, 2013

RESOLUTION NO.             R66-13




Ghida S. Neukirch, City Clerk

                REQUEST FOR PLAN COMMISSION ACTION


DATE REFERRED:                   November 19, 2013

ORIGINATED BY:                   Department of Community Development

SUBJECT:        Concurrent Public Hearings for 807- 833 Laurel Avenue:

                Public Hearing 12-05-REZ-001 for a proposed Zoning Map Amendment from RM1A
                Medium-to-High Density Multiple Family Residential District to RO High Density
                Residential/Office District; and,

                Public Hearing 12-05-PUD-002 for a Special Use in the Nature of a Preliminary and
                Final Planned Development with Subdivision (12-05-SUB-002) for a Proposed 52-Unit
                Multiple Family Building to be Constructed in Two Phases, with Requested
                Modifications from the Zoning Requirements Regulating Front and Side Yard Setback,
                Building Height, and Lot Coverage.

SUMMARY AND BACKGROUND OF SUBJECT MATTER:

The applicant in this matter, Fulton Developers (Fulton), is the owner of the properties located at 807,
819, 825, and 833 Laurel Avenue. Fulton is proposing to develop a 52 unit multiple-family building in
two phases.

Plan Commission Process: Based on the nature of the proposed development, the applicant will be
requesting the following approvals from the City of Highland Park:

    -   Zoning Map Amendment from the RM1A Medium-to-High Density to the RO High Density
        Residential/Office zoning district (Zoning Code Article XV
    -   Subdivision of the subject property into a single lot (City Code Chapter 151);
    -   Special Use in the Nature of a Planned Development (concurrent Preliminary and Final
        consideration) with modifications (Zoning Code Articles V and XIV)

In addition to Plan Commission consideration, the Design Review Commission will review the exterior
design features of the building and landscape design; the Housing Commission will review the affordable
housing aspects of the proposed development in advance of Plan Commission's final recommendation
and City Council consideration.

The demolition of the existing single family houses does not require Historic Preservation Commission
review because structures in the RM1A zoning district are not subject to demolition review/delay.

Subject Property: The site is located on the north side of Laurel Avenue, between McGovern and
Hickory Streets, which is situated to the west of downtown Highland Park and is included in the Central
District planning area. Laurel Avenue is a primary arterial roadway connecting downtown to U.S.
Highway 41 and destinations to the west. The property is zoned in the RM1A multiple family zoning
district, 22 du/ac, with no commercial uses permitted. Permitted density in the RO zoning district along
and east of Green Bay Road is 50 dwelling units per acre. Further west and south of the subject property
are a range of lower density zoning districts including RM1 Multiple Family (15 du/ac); R6 (6 du/ac); R5
(3.5 du/ac); and, R4 Single Family (2 du/ac).




                                                                                                           1
                REQUEST FOR PLAN COMMISSION ACTION




 To date, only the adjacent 15-unit Laurel Court Phase I townhome development has been developed in the
 RM1A zoning district, where the subject property is located. That project was approved by City Council
 in 2006 and constructed in 2007.

The proposed development was twice presented to the Plan Commission in pre-application discussions
sessions. In May 2012 the applicant presented a very similar plan including rezoning of the subject
property. In December 2012 the applicant proposed a similar plan but was no longer requesting that the
property be rezoned and was instead looking for direction from the Plan Commission on a project
including 52 units to be constructed on the subject property through proposed amendment to provisions of
the Planned Development process.

Proposed Zoning Map Amendment  Comparison of Zoning District Requirements

In order to develop the subject property to the proposed 52 units, which would exceed the allowable
density under the current zoning, the developer is seeking to have the zoning of the subject site changed
from the current RM1A district to the RO zoning district. Under the RM1A zoning district the maximum
number of dwelling units that can be built, inclusive of all bonuses for providing affordable housing under
the requirements of the inclusionary housing regulations is 25. In comparison, with an RO zoning
designation the maximum number of units that can be developed inclusive of bonuses is 53.

The differences between the current and proposed zoning regulations are shown in the following table:

                                             Existing RM1A                        Proposed RO
Minimum Average Width                              50 ft                              50 ft
Minimum Lot Area for MF Use                    21,780 sq ft                        21,780 sq ft
Minimum Lot Area per DU                        1,980 sq ft                          871 sq ft
Permitted Density                               22 du/ac                            50 du/ac
Minimum Front Yard                                 10 ft                              25 ft

                REQUEST FOR PLAN COMMISSION ACTION

Minimum Rear Yard                       10 ft; or 20 if adjacent to a      20 ft; or 20% of Lot Depth,
                                             residential district                whichever is less
Maximum Height                         40 ft; maximum of 3 stories                     45 ft
Maximum Lot Coverage                               33.3%                              33.3%

Standards for a Zoning Map Amendment  Set Forth in Article XV of the Zoning Code

In this matter, the subject site zoning is paramount. The Commission must make a recommendation to the
City Council in support of the proposed zoning map amendment if it is to make a favorable
recommendation for the proposed Planned Development. In consideration of this matter, the Commission
must take the following standards into account when considering the proposed Zoning Map Amendment:

    1. The existing uses and zoning of nearby properties;
    2. The extent to which property values are diminished by the existing zoning;
    3. The extent to which the existing zoning and/or proposed zoning promotes the general health,
       safety, and welfare of the citizenry of the City;
    4. The relative gain to the public as compared to the hardship imposed upon the petitioner;
    5. The suitability of the subject property for the purposes for which it is presently zoned;
    6. The length of time that the subject property has been vacant, as presently zoned, considered in the
       context of the land development in the area in which the property is located;
    7. The compatibility of existing zoning as compared to the compatibility of the proposed zoning
       with the existing Master Plan; and
    8. The evidence or lack of evidence of community need for the use proposed by the petitioner which
       would require the zoning amendment.

                                                                                                         5
                REQUEST FOR PLAN COMMISSION ACTION


Proposed Planned Development

The developer has applied for a special use in the nature of a planned development to allow for the
construction of the 52-unit multiple family development project, to be completed in two phases. At this
time the developer is seeking both Preliminary and Final Planned Development approval. Each
development phase would be developed on 19,000 square feet of land area and contain 26 total units.
After completion of the first phase the building would contain 22 market rate units and 4 affordable units.
The project phasing of the Planned Development is as follows:

Phase I: 26 dwellings units in the westernmost portion of the building, 50% of the parking structure and
the retention of the two existing houses located at 807 and 819 Laurel Avenue.




Phase II: Demolition of the existing single family residences and construction of the balance of the
building including 26 additional dwelling units for a total of 52 and the remaining 50% of the
underground parking structure.




                                                                                                           6
                REQUEST FOR PLAN COMMISSION ACTION




Although the street level appearance of the development will appear as two buildings, the underground
parking garage will be beneath the entirety of the development with doors and openings from the two
phases into the singular space of the garage. The communication of these doors an opening into the
common garage is, by the zoning code definition of "Building," one building, not two separate buildings.

Planned Development Standards

Pursuant to Section 150.520 Site Planning Constraints and Design Standards, The applicant for a
Planned Development must demonstrate to the Plan Commission and the City Council that the
proposed Planned Development satisfies and incorporates, to the greatest extent practicable, the
following site design standards which, where applicable have been evaluated by the Department
of Community Development in the bolded text following the standards:

(A)    Protection of the Public Health, Safety, and Welfare. The uses and structures within the
Planned Development shall be compatible with one another, in that they are designed, located,
and proposed to be operated so that the public health, safety and welfare will be protected.

(B)     Preservation of Environmentally Sensitive Areas.

(1)     No development shall occur in any Environmentally Sensitive Area located on the subject
property, except upon approval of a modification therefore, in accordance with Section
150.510(B) of this Article. (No environmentally sensitive areas have been indentified on the
site.)




                                                                                                           7
                 REQUEST FOR PLAN COMMISSION ACTION

(2)     Environmentally Sensitive Areas located on the subject property may be included as
common open space within a Planned Development, upon either (a) identification of such areas
on the plat of subdivision as a separate lot or lots, or (b) recordation by the applicant of a
conservation easement or similar restriction that ensures the preservation of such areas, in
perpetuity, from future development. (No environmentally sensitive areas are found or
included as common open space in the proposed development plan.)

(C)      Historic Resources. The Planned Development shall preserve all (1) locally designated
landmarks, and (2) properties, structures, areas, objects, and landscapes determined to be
historically significant by the Historic Preservation Commission in accordance with Chapters 24
or 170 of the Code. (No historic resources are found on the subject property. The homes
proposed to be demolished are exempt from Demolition Delay review by the Historic
Preservation Commission.

(D)     Clustering New Development. The Planned Development shall preserve the structures,
landscapes, scenic view sheds, and other natural and historic features of the subject property,
through (i) clustering of lots or building pads, (ii) adaptive reuse of existing structures, and (iii)
the protection of designated open space from development; provided, however, that clustering of
development shall not be required upon a demonstration by the applicant, to the satisfaction of the
Plan Commission and the City Council, that there are no features on the subject property worthy
of preservation, or that those features worthy of preservation will be more effectively preserved
by not clustering development.

All clustering shall be designed in accordance with the following standards:

       (1)     Lots shall be configured to minimize the length of roadways required for the
proposed Planned Development.

       (2)     Building envelopes shall be configured to minimize the loss of, and damage to,
Environmentally Sensitive Areas located on the subject property.

        (3)     All residential units shall be grouped into clusters, in accordance with the
following:

                (a)   Each cluster shall contain not less than three dwelling units, and not
more than 10 single-family detached dwelling units nor more than 20 of all other types of
dwelling units.

                (b)    To the extent practicable, residential clusters shall be located so as to (i)
minimize negative impacts on the natural and cultural resources on the site, (ii) minimize
conflicts between incompatible uses, (iii) minimize disturbance to Environmentally Sensitive
Areas, and (iv) protect existing historic buildings and landscapes. (Not applicable as the
development is not proposed to be clustered.)

The building clustering requirements set forth above are not applicable to the proposed
development. No new roadways are proposed by the applicant and there are no environmentally
sensitive features present to be preserved through clustering.)

(E)     Location of Structures. All structures to be located within the Planned Development shall
(1) be related harmoniously to the terrain and to existing structures in the vicinity of the subject




                                                                                                         8
                  REQUEST FOR PLAN COMMISSION ACTION

property, and (2) have a visual relationship to existing nearby structures; (The proposed
multiple-family building is located in an area characterized by multiple family land use.)

(F)     Environmental Quality and Responsible Design. The Planned Development shall be
consistent with the City of Highland Park Environmental Policy and with the City of Highland
Park Checklist for Environmentally Responsible Design and Construction. The applicant may
demonstrate consistency with standards established for site design and building construction
practices by referencing known sustainable development and green architecture rating systems.
(The applicant will address these design issues at the public hearing)

(G)      Preservation of Landscapes. The landscapes within the Planned Development shall be
preserved in their natural states, insofar as practicable, by minimizing tree and soil removal. All
proposed grade changes shall be consistent with the general appearance of neighboring developed
areas. (The applicant will be removing all of the trees from the subject property. In advance
of any tree removal, the applicant will be notified of the obligations for tree replacement
under the requirements of the City of Highland Park Code.)

(H)    Schools, Parks, and Public Facilities. The Planned Development shall not impose an
undue burden on parks, recreational areas, schools, or other public facilities that serve or are
proposed to serve the Planned Development. (To be determined by the Plan Commission.)

The estimated population and student generation for the development is the following 2

(I)      Relationship and Connection to Adjoining Land. The Planned Development shall not be
designed as an enclave separate from adjacent properties, unless existing development patterns,
natural features, and/or topographic conditions prevent vehicular or pedestrian access connections
to adjacent properties. In order to achieve connectivity to adjoining land, all lots, streets,
sidewalks and/or paths within a Planned Development shall be designed, to the extent practicable,
to allow for the continuation of such existing or proposed features to adjoining areas. New
streets, sidewalks, and/or paths located within a proposed Planned Development shall be
constructed and installed to the boundaries of the proposed Planned Development if the City
Council determines, in its sole discretion, that the proposed Planned Development adjoins land
with the potential of being subdivided or resubdivided. (The proposed development exists
within an already developed area that is accessible by pedestrians to many community
facilities including downtown Highland Park and major recreation and civic facilities.)

(K)     Functional and Mechanical Features. Exposed storage areas, trash containers, recycling
container space, exposed machinery installations, service areas, truck loading areas, utility
buildings and structures, and similar accessory areas and structures shall be (1) identified on the
site plan required pursuant to Section 150.525(A)(9) of this Chapter, (2) incorporated into
common areas of the development, (3) made as unobtrusive as possible, and (4) designed,
landscaped, and screened in accordance with the requirements set forth in Article XXII of this
Chapter and of Chapter 176 of the Code. (The proposed trash storage area is located off the
alley and is illustrated as being screened in the submitted plans.)

(L)      Distance Between Buildings. The minimum horizontal distance between any two new
buildings to be located on the subject property, or between any new building and an existing
building (including building appurtenances), shall be not less than 15 feet; provided, however,
that this Section 150.520(L) shall not apply to buildings that (1) share a common wall, and (2)
have individual entrances and exits. (The proposed development meets this standard.)

(M)      Surface Water Drainage. In accordance with the stormwater management regulations set
forth in Article XVIII of this Chapter, surface drainage systems serving the subject property shall
be designed to prevent surface waters from adversely affecting neighboring properties or the
public stormwater drainage system. Surface water in all paved areas shall be collected at intervals
so as to prevent obstruction of the flow of vehicular or pedestrian traffic. The design of the




                                                                                                         11
                REQUEST FOR PLAN COMMISSION ACTION

stormwater management system shall enhance natural stormwater storage areas such as high-
quality aquatic resources and regulatory floodplains, and may incorporate natural stormwater
management techniques commonly referred to as low impact development techniques or best
management practices. (The proposed plans do not show the provision of stormwater
detention facilities. The Engineering Division is currently reviewing the submitted plans
and applicant calculations and the City Code (Watershed Development Ordinance) to
determine whether stormwater detention facilities are required. Additional information
may be available at the public hearing.)

(N)     Ingress to and egress from the Planned Development shall be designed to (1) promote safe
vehicular movements, (2) minimize traffic congestion in the public streets outside the Planned
Development, and (3) facilitate the free flow of vehicular and pedestrian traffic within the Planned
Development.

(Vehicular access into and out of the development is all off of the public alley to the rear of the
property. This is an actively used alley providing access to commercial uses on Central Avenue and
residential uses on Laurel and McGovern in addition to being a part of the parking pick-up and
drop-off area for the Bethany Methodist Church and daycare program located on Laurel and
McGovern. The applicant has submitted a Traffic Impact Study (attached), prepared by Gewalt
Hamilton Associates, Inc. The consultant's conclusion is as follows:

                Based on our observations and analyses we feel that the existing alley
                and roadway networks can readily accommodate the traffic generations
                associated with this type of residential development with the
                implementation of the recommended traffic operations plan.
                Furthermore, it is our finding that the proposed parking supply is more
                than sufficient to meet the City's criteria and could be further reduced
                to potentially provide additional public space or wider marked spaces
                for guests and residents.

Gewalt Hamilton Associates has recommended the following actions to accommodate the
residential traffic associated with the Laurel Court II development.

            -   The new site access should be under Stop Sign control
            -   One inbound and one outbound lane should be provided at the site access.)

Subdivision Standards

The following section reviews the compliance of the proposed Plat of Subdivision with City Code Section
151.004 Minimum Design Standards of Subdivisions.

(A)     Lots.

(1) Lot shapes. Every lot shall have four sides. (Proposed development meets this standard)

(2) Lot depths. The minimum depth of lots shall be 125 feet. (Proposed development meets this
standard)

(3) Conformance with Zoning Ordinance.

(a)     Minimum lot area and average lot width. Minimum lot area and average lot width shall
correspond to the zoning regulations of the district within which the land being subdivided is located and
the minimum design standards set forth herein.
(Proposed subdivision meets this standard.)

(b)     Existing structures. A subdivision shall not be approved when said subdivision places an existing
permanent structure in violation of the requirements of the Zoning Ordinance or the minimum design
standards of this Chapter. (Proposed subdivision meets this standard)

(c)     Planned Unit Developments. In conjunction with the review required under Section 150.506 of
this Code, no subdivision into two or more parts of a tract of land that is three or more acres shall be
approved, except in compliance with this Chapter and with the planned unit development review and
approval process required by Article V, Chapter 150 of this Code, including, without limitation, the
requirement under Subsection 150.503(B) of this Code that any residential development on, or
subdivision of, a tract of land of three or more acres must be developed under the planned unit
development regulations. (Project is being developed as a Planned Development)

(4)    Required area of tableland. Each proposed lot shall contain at least 20 percent tableland.
(Proposed subdivision meets this standard)

(5)     Relationship to streets. Each lot shall have principal frontage on a public street. Through lots are
prohibited. (Proposed subdivision meets this standard)

(6)     Established Property Width Average. In a single-or two-family residential zoning district, if sixty
percent (60%) or more of the properties fronting on one side of a block located in the same zoning district
have widths greater than the minimum lot width required in that zoning district, then the average property
width of the existing properties shall be deemed to be the established property for such block (Not
applicable)

(B)     Streets and Alleys and Pedestrian Ways. The plat of the proposed subdivision shall provide for
dedication of the necessary land for public streets and alleys proposed by the plat or projected by the
Master Plan. (Not applicable).

(2)     Street relationships, connections, and dead-end streets (cul-de-sacs). (Not applicable)

development meets this standard)

(C)       Other Public Use Areas and Public Use Facilities. In accord with the Master Plan, the plat of the

such easements from block to block. In addition, the plat of the proposed subdivision shall provide for

been evaluated by the City Engineer  see comments in this report.).

Utility Line Burial Requirements
Except as otherwise provided, all utility distribution lines for telephone, gas, electric,
telecommunications, internet, or cable television services (collectively referred to in this Section as
"Utility Lines") to be newly installed, or to be reinstalled from existing overhead facilities, shall be placed
underground within easements or dedicated public rights-of-way. Specifically, and without limitation of
the foregoing, all overhead Utility Lines located on property that is the subject of an application for
subdivision approval pursuant to this Subdivision Code, or on a public right-of-way adjacent to such
property, shall, as a condition of such subdivision approval, be placed underground within a dedicated
easement or a public right-of-way.

(The applicant is seeking relief from this requirement so that they do not have to bury the existing
overhead utility lines in the alley behind the subject property.)


Identified Planned Development Relief: The Planned Development regulations allow for the approval
of developments wherein the underlying zoning requirements for the subject zoning district may be
modified. The only prohibited modifications relate to the following and the applicant is not seeking any
such modifications:

    -   Modifications to the permitted uses in the zoning district;
    -   Modifications that result in the increase of density; and
    -   Modifications that would permit future development in a land banked area within any part of the
        approved common open space.

At the present time, staff has identified the following modifications from the underlying zoning standards
of the RO zoning district requirements:




                                                                                                            21
                REQUEST FOR PLAN COMMISSION ACTION

    -   To allow encroachment of the front and side setbacks;
    -   To reduce required side yard setback for building height in excess of 15 feet
    -   To allow buildings taller than 45 feet
    -   To allow lot coverage greater than 33.3%;
    -   To reduce the parking stall and drive aisle module length from the required 61'-6"

Inclusionary Housing Requirements: Section 150.2101 requires the provision of permanently
constructed affordable housing units on-site for developments of 5 or more residential units. While
Article 21 of the Zoning Code does provide alternatives to the production of on-site units, it is the intent
and preference of the policy to encourage privately produced, owned, and managed affordable housing
units. Article 21 requires that a total of 20% of the total number of residential units are affordable. The
applicant is proposing 22 market rate and 4 affordable units per phase, or 44 market rate and 8 affordable
units in total. The proposal meets the inclusionary housing requirements of Article XXI for the number of
units provided. Pursuant to City process, the applicant will be directed to meet with City professional staff
and submit an inclusionary housing plan to the Housing Commission for its consideration and
recommendation to the City Council in conjunction with the processing of the proposed Planned
Development.

Master Plan Recommendations: Per the Master Plan that was adopted by the City in 2001, the subject
site is located within the Central Planning District. As previously noted the zoning of the subject site in
the RM1A district was an action taken to implement the concept of transitional residential land use of the
subject block. The Central District Plan did not recommend expanding the RO Residential Office zoning
district beyond the locations where it is currently applied.

Engineering Division Preliminary Review Comments:

The Engineering Division reviewed the submitted plans and offered the following comments:

-   The project engineer must submit a calculation of the existing and proposed impervious areas for this
    development to determine the necessity of stormwater detention facilities on-site. (Submitted and
    under review with the Engineering Division)

-   The proposed development is tributary to the Central Avenue sanitary sewer. The engineer must
    submit a calculation of the existing capacity of the Central Avenue sanitary sewer, between Elmwood
    Drive and Beverly Place, in order to determine if it has sufficient capacity to serve the proposed
    development plus the existing sanitary sewage volume. (Not yet submitted)

-   The proposed plan includes a parallel parking bay on Laurel Avenue. On-street parking is prohibited
    between 819 Laurel Avenue and Hickory Street. The proposed parking bay will eliminate the existing
    parkway, including existing lawn and trees, and is not deemed necessary by the Department of Public
    Works. The proposed parking bay will interfere with snow removal.

-   The two existing utility poles in the alley north of the development and the existing pole near Hickory
    Street, that was not required to be removed during the construction of Laurel Court I, should be
    reviewed relative to the requirement for burial of utility lines as part of the subdivision process.
    (Variation from Subdivision requirements requested)

OVERVIEW

The property is located within Highland Park's Downtown District along Laurel Avenue, just over a
block west of Green Bay Road. The current zoning district is RM1A, which allows for multifamily
residential. The site is bound by a public alley running along the north side of the property with a
combination of retail, commercial and office uses under the B4 Commercial Zoning. On the south side
along Laurel Avenue, there are multifamily residential units currently under construction. The Laurel
Court Row Homes, which were developed by the applicant Fulton Developers, can be found adjacent to
the property on the west side.

The property consists of 4 lots with residences with no architectural value which not only create a sharp
contrast with the surrounding developed downtown but also diminish the value of the surrounding
properties. Two of the homes have recently been demolished..

Laurel Avenue is considered one of the "character streets" for the Central District and also serves as one
of the City's main arteries to access downtown. Therefore, any improvement on this street would benefit
the whole community in addition to the immediate neighbors.

The proposed development consists of two multiple family residential buildings each consisting of 22
market rate units and 4 affordable units. The project will have an underground parking garage, a green
roof and an open plaza at the rear, all part of the common areas.

Since the start of the recession in 2008, the Real Estate market has experienced a few drastic changes.
Leaving aside the evident decrease in home prices and sales, the size of newly built homes has fallen for
the first time in decades. In addition to the recession, there are several factors that have contributed to
this new tendency such as increase in energy costs, concerns about affordability, tight credit for big
mortgages and aging baby boomers, all of which have not been an exception in Highland Park. We feel
that a new multifamily residential development needs to address the market's demand for smaller and
more efficient units which cannot be achieved in a successful way through the existing RM1A zoning.



                                                     2
Laurel Court, which was developed under the RM1A zoning has 15 town homes that range mostly
between 3,000 and 4,000 square feet. Although we are proud to acknowledge that this project has been a
success, we are certain that we would not achieve a positive outcome by developing a similar project in
the neighboring property because we would not be meeting the market's demand for smaller units. In
addition, due the nature of this type of development with underground parking, and ample common
areas, it would not be feasible to simply reduce the size of the units and still have a successful project.
Needless to say, if we reduce the size of the units, the quantity of units would have to increase otherwise
the revenue from the sale of those units would merely pay for the construction of the proposed common
areas and underground parking.

We therefore believe that the RM1A needs to be amended to address the market's demand for smaller
units and at the same time comply with the main goals contemplated by the Central District Plan.

The Proposed amendment will have minimal impact, since neither the bulk, number of bedrooms or
traffic will be increased when comparing with what we can build under the current RM1A zoning
district. The main modifications take place in the interior of the building to better respond to the markets
demands for smaller units.


MODIFICATIONS FROM ZONING DISTRCT STANDARDS

       1- MODIFY THE RM1A ZONING TO RO


REASONS FOR AMENDMENT:

   A- The amendment is consistent with the recommendations provided by The Lakota Group for the
      downtown district.

   B- The property is within the boundaries of Downtown Highland Park and as stated in the 2001
      Central District Plan and reinstated in the Vision Statement prepared in 2011, which is part of the
      Central District Master Plan update, we should "encourage high density multiple family
      development within the downtown...is one of the means of responding to market demands for
      such housing and reserving land in the surrounding neighborhoods for other land uses".

   C- The entire RM1A district consists of our property and 4 more adjacent parcels which make the
      change relatively simple.

   D- Market's demand for smaller units within the downtown.

   E- There is excellent transportation accessibility within the downtown Highland Park and we should
      therefore encourage more residents to use it within the area.




                                                     3
   F- By promoting population growth within the downtown it will benefit the downtown businesses
      as well as the future residents who will have all of the services the downtown has to offer within
      walking distance.

   G- There used to be smaller condominiums and apartments built in the past such as those along
      Central Av above the retail area and in the Ravinia along Roger Williams, which are less than
      half the size of the ones that what we are proposing.

As seen in the drawing below,

THE PROPOSED FOOTPRINT AND BUILDING BOX REMAIN SIMILAR AS TO WHAT IS
ALLOWED UNDER THE RM1A. THE AMOUNT OF BEDROOMS WILL BE ABOUT THE SAME.




     23 UNITS WITH AN AVERAGE OF                           52 UNITS WITH AN AVERAGE OF
                3,200 SF                                              1,300 SF
    TOTAL OF 72 BEDROOMS OR MORE                               TOTAL OF 72 BEDROOMS


                                                   4
       2- BUILDING HEIGHT:

The building to the west at a height of 42' 11 " complies with the 45 feet maximum height of the RO
zoning. The building to the east at 45'11 " would require minimal relief.

REASONS FOR RELIEF:


   1. We are measuring height based on the height definition of the entire lot. However, due to the
      relative large difference in grade between the east and west side of the lot, if we were to consider
      that each building has its own property, they would both comply with the 45 feet height
      limitation and no relief would be necessary.

   2. The 4th floor is stepped back along Laurel Avenue, thus creating the appearance of a shorter
      building.

   3. The existing topography of the RM1A should be taken into consideration with the surrounding
      context. There is a 40 foot drop between Green Bay Road and the subject property which
      provides an opportunity to increase the height without affecting the character of the Downtown.

   4. The height restriction not only limits the interior ceiling height but also the design options. We
      would be able to comply with the height restriction by simply providing 8 foot ceilings. This
      would provide however, a non-desirable and less marketable project and also limit the design
      options.

   5. In addition, over 50% of the building is setback an additional 4'-6" beyond the 10 foot front
      setback, visually minimizing the bulk of the building.


       3- FRONT SETBACK
          Laurel Court directly to the west has a 10ft front setback and therefore the proposed 10ft
          front setback is consistent with the neighboring property.

       4- MAXIMIM LOT COVERAGE

We have noticed that all of the multiple family projects approved in Highland Park within the downtown
area exceed the lot coverage requirement of 33,3%. This restriction, might be reasonable for properties
that are further away from the downtown district, however based on the approved projects by the
Planning Commission and the City Council most of the projects within the downtown district have a lot
coverage closer to 50%. We are proposing a 51.7% lot coverage which is consistent with projects within
the downtown.

In no particular order the following is the lot coverage of some similar projects:

847 Laurel Av - Laurel Court: 50.4%



                                                     5
2021 St Johns  Le Maisons: 47,8%
2000 Green Bay Road:        44,3%
650 Laurel Av:              53,4%

         5- MAINTAIN ELECTRIC POWER LINES ALONG ALLEY

We request relief from removing the 3 electrical power lines along the alley.
  1. This is an alley and the power lines are not visible from the street.
  2. The power lines along the 3 poles adjacent to our property, serve mainly the commercial
      buildings along Central Avenue. There are overhead transformers on each one of the poles
      serving those properties and therefore in order to remove the poles, we would have to do
      underground work on other properties and find a location on the ground to relocate those
      transformers. It wouldn't be possible to relocate the transformers on this other properties and we
      should not lose ground area or parking spaces to relocate other properties transformers on our
      property.
  3. In order to remove the 3 electrical poles along the alley a new pole would have to be installed at
      the east corner of the property.
  4. When building Laurel Court, it wasn't possible to remove one of the electrical poles along the
      alley because it was also serving a commercial property along Central Av (the post office and the
      bank). There are therefore 2 poles in front of Laurel Court that could not be removed.


         6- PARKING

We have been able to prepare an underground parking plan as seen on Sheet A4-A, that complies with
on-site parking requirements.
However, in order to provide parking spaces that are a little bit wider than code, we are proposing to
build the underground parking plan on sheet A4-B which has 3 parking spaces less on each building.
We are therefore proposing a total of 92 parking spaces.

REASONS FOR RELIEF:

   1- To be able to provide wider than code parking spaces.
   2- Based on the parking study prepared by Gewalt Hamilton and Associates, the project is within
      1,000 feet of public transportation. It would therefore be eligible for the Alternative Parking
      Reduction discount of 15% which would suggest that only 83 spaces would be required. We are
      proposing 92 parking spaces.

                                                   7
PUBLIC BENEFIT

Based on the City's plans to provide a bicycle lane along Laurel Av, we would make a financial
contribution for the cost of the bicycle lane along Laurel Avenue between Mc. Govern and Hickory
Street.

The building will have a green roof (which would be the first one in Highland Park) along with several
other sustainable and energy efficient features.


CONCLUSION

When comparing what is allowed under the current RM1A zoning district and what we are proposing, it
is clear that there would be no major differences when looking at the project from the exterior. The only
purpose of the proposed modifications is to provide a project that's marketable, since there is currently
no demand for 3,000 to 4,000 square foot units.

The bulk and footprint of the building would be not only about the same size as what is allowed under
the current zoning but since we are also pushing the building back on certain areas it would further
minimize the bulk. We are also proposing 2 buildings instead of one, which will provide the appearance
of a smaller building.

The amount of bedrooms would be about the same or less than the ones we are allowed to do by right.

The proposed project would also have an underground parking, which is one of the goals under the 2001
Central district Plan and 2011 Vision Plan for all new residential developments downtown.

The relief we are seeking is consistent with the Master Plan, the 2001 Central District Plan, the new
2011 Vision Plan and the Lakota Group study for downtown and provides a more viable way of
achieving its goals.

With all due respect, we would kindly ask you to consider the plans submitted and in turn, submit a
favorable recommendation to the City Council.
