TRAFFIC IMPACT STUDY
To:            Mr. Mark Muller
               Fulton Developers

From:          Daniel P. Brinkman, P.E., PTOE
               Amanda L. Larson, P.E.I.

Date:          October 4, 2013

Subject:       Proposed Residential Development
               Laurel Court II
               807-833 Laurel Avenue
               Highland Park, IL


                                 PART I INTRODUCTION & SUMMARY STATEMENT

GEWALT HAMILTON ASSOCIATES, INC. (GHA) has conducted a traffic impact study for the above referenced project.
Fulton Developers proposes to re-develop several residential lots along Laurel Avenue into a multi-unit
development. The subject site of Laurel Court II is located east of Laurel Court along the north side of Laurel
Avenue east of Hickory Avenue in Highland Park, IL.

The following analysis is intended to flow from a review of the existing conditions through the proposed plan while
highlighting our approach, methodology, and findings, ultimately providing various recommendations for your
consideration. Briefly summarizing, the additional traffic generated by the proposed residential development can be
readily accommodated by the existing alley system, as well as the area roadways with few additional roadway
improvements.

Exhibits and Appendices referenced in the following text are conveniently located in the Technical Addendum at the
end of this document.

                                      PART II BACKGROUND INFORMATION

Site Location Map and Photo Inventory

      Exhibit 1 provides a location map of the site vicinity and Exhibit 2 provides photo inventory of operations in the
      vicinity of the subject site. Pertinent comments include:

           The subject site is approximately 0.9 acres in total and is located along the north side of Laurel Avenue,
           east of Hickory Avenue in the City of Highland Park.
           Laurel Avenue is considered a minor arterial along the site frontage and is under the jurisdiction of the City
           of Highland Park.
           Along the subject site, Laurel provides one travel lane in each direction and parking on both sides of the
           road. Parking on the south side of Laurel is limited to 3-hours and parking on the north side is metered.
           There are two metered spaces along the eastern edge of the site frontage.
           As Laurel approaches its signalized intersection with Hickory / Deerfield Road a separate eastbound left
           turn lane is provided in addition to the single through lanes.
                                                                     Proposed Residential Development  Laurel Court II
                                                                                                807-833 Laurel Avenue
                                                                                                     Highland Park, IL
        Hickory Street is a local (City of Highland Park) route extending from Central Avenue to Laurel Avenue,
        providing a single travel lane in each direction. Parking is prohibited on both sides of Hickory.
        The northern limit of the subject site is an approximately 20-foot wide public alley referred to as Central
        Court. This alley parallels Central and intersects another public alley northeast of the subject site. Adjacent
        developments including several retail, offices, and the Laurel Court I residential developments have access
        directly to the alley.

    See Appendix I, for an aerial photo of the subject site and surrounding development.

Existing Traffic

    Exhibit 3 summarizes the existing Weekday Morning and Evening Peak Hour traffic volumes in the site vicinity.
    Weekday Peak Period (6-9 AM and 3-6 PM) counts were conducted by GHA on Thursday, September 19th at
    the Laurel Avenue / Hickory Street intersection as well as the Hickory Street intersection with Central Court and
    the Alley intersections surrounding the site.

    The observed Peak Hours occurred from 7:45 to 8:45 AM and 4:30 to 5:30 PM.

    No unusual activities (e.g. emergency vehicle activity, roadway construction, etc) or inclement weather were
    observed during our counts that would be expected to impact traffic volumes or travel patterns in the vicinity.

    Summaries of the existing traffic counts can be found in Appendix II.

                                        PART III PROPOSED DEVELOPMENT

Site Plan

    Exhibit 4 consists of the May 6, 2013 site plan for the proposed Laurel Court II development. As previously
    noted, Fulton Developers intend to construct two buildings in separate phases that will ultimately total 52
    dwelling units. All units will have underground parking accessed from the alley / Central Court. Additionally, a
    total of 13 guest parking spaces along the alley are proposed as well as four spaces along Laurel Avenue in
    front of the main lobby entrance. An additional 5 alley spaces are going to be assigned to the building across
    the alley from the subject site.

Project Traffic Characteristics

    Exhibit 5  Part A tabulates the anticipated traffic generations for the proposed development, based on trip rate
    data published by the Institute of Transportation Engineers (ITE) in the most recent, 9th Edition of the manual
    Trip Generation using Residential Condominium / Townhouse (Land Use #230. As can be seen, the
    development is expected to generate approximately 30 trips (combined entering and exiting) during both the
    Morning and Evening Peak Hours and approximately 290 trips on a Daily or 24-hour basis.




                                                                        GEWALT HAMILTON ASSOCIATES, INC.  Page 2
                                                                    Proposed Residential Development  Laurel Court II
                                                                                               807-833 Laurel Avenue
                                                                                                    Highland Park, IL
   Exhibit 5  Part B provides the anticipated trip distribution, which is primarily based on the existing traffic
   volumes and patterns observed in the site area. As can be seen, it is anticipated that a majority of the traffic
   with be oriented to/from the west on Laurel Avenue. Ultimately, trip distribution will be based on where residents
   work, shop and travel to.

Traffic Assignments

   Exhibit 6 illustrates the anticipated site traffic volumes generated by the full buildout (52 dwelling units) which
   have been assigned to the area roadway network based on the project's traffic characteristics as discussed
   above and summarized in Exhibit 5 (i.e. traffic generations and trip distribution) and the site access system.

   A 2% growth factor was applied to Existing through traffic (see Exhibit 3) to reflect other non-project traffic
   growth during the phased construction period and then combined with the Site traffic (Exhibit 6) resulting in the
   Total Traffic assignment, which is presented in Exhibit 7.

                                              PART IV EVALUATION

Intersection Capacity Analyses

   Capacity Analyses were conducted at the intersections within the study area. The analysis parameters utilized
   are listed in Part A, as published in the Transportation research Board's (TRB) 2010 Highway Capacity Manual
   (HCM). At signalized intersections, Level of Service (LOS) "reports" traffic operations using the letter
   designations "A" (best) through "F" (worst) and measures the "control delay" per vehicle in seconds. LOS C is
   often referred to as intersection "design" guideline and LOS D is usually considered as providing the lower
   threshold of "acceptable" operations. LOS E and F are usually considered "unacceptable".

   At unsignalized intersections, the HCM methodology reports the results differently for Two-Way Stop Controlled
   (TWSC) or All-Way Stop Controlled (AWSC) intersections. For TWSC intersections, LOS is reported for
   conflicting movements on the major street (i.e. left turns onto the minor approach) and for each movement on
   the stopped approach. Approach "control delay" is also reported in seconds per vehicle. Results of AWSC
   analyses are slightly different. LOS is reported for each stopped approach as well as an average overall
   intersection "control delay" in seconds per vehicle. LOS C and D continue to be considered "design" and
   "acceptable" operations respectively.

   Exhibit 9 Part B. summarizes the intersection capacity analysis results for the Weekday Morning and Evening
   Peak Hours. As can be seen, the additional traffic generated by the Laurel Court II development is expected to
   have a negligible impact on the adjacent roadways and intersection operations. All individual movements and
   intersections will continue to operate at or above the "design" LOS C during both of the analyzed Peak Hours
   with little or no recommended improvements. At the signalized intersection of Laurel Avenue and Hickory
   Street, it would be recommended that a westbound left turn lane be striped in the existing painted median.

   The Highway Capacity Software (HCS) summary printouts are provided as Appendix III for reference.

                                                                     Proposed Residential Development  Laurel Court II
                                                                                                807-833 Laurel Avenue
                                                                                                     Highland Park, IL
                                 PART V RECOMMENDATIONS AND CONCLUSIONS

Traffic Operations Plan

Exhibit 9 schematically illustrates the recommendations to accommodate the residential traffic associated with the
Laurel Court II development. Key components include the following:

        The new site access should be under Stop Sign control
        One inbound and one outbound lane should be provided at the site access.

Parking Calculations

    Per the City's Zoning Ordinance, different sizes and types of multi-family dwelling units require different parking
    standards: 1.25 spaces for studio, 1.5 spaces for 1 bedroom, 2 spaces for 2 or more bedroom units, and an
    additional 0.25 spaces of guest parking for buildings with more than 5 units.

    Each of the Laurel Court II buildings are expected to have 16 1 bedroom and 10 2 bedroom units. Furthermore,
    one unit on each level (4 per building) will be considered an "Affordable Housing" unit. The Following
    summarizes the parking calculations per ordinance:

    16 1-bedroom x 1.5 spaces = 24
    10 2-bedroom x 2 spaces = 20
    21 units x 0.25 guest spaces =5.5 ~ 5 (note only "market rate" units must provide guest parking)
    Total = 49 spaces for each building or a total of 98 spaces.

    City ordinance allows for a 15% reduction in parking for units within 1,000 feet of a commuter train station or
    regular bus route. PACE route 471 has regular stops along Central Avenue and Laurel Avenue within this
    distance. While the current site plan proposes 104 spaces (not including the 5 for the adjacent development
    across the alley) plus 4 spaces along Laurel Avenue it is eligible for the Alternative Transportation Reduction
    discount suggesting that only 83 spaces are required.

Conclusion

Based on our observations and analyses we feel that the existing alley and roadway networks can readily
accommodate the traffic generations associated with this type of residential development with the implementation of
the recommended traffic operations plan. Furthermore, it is our finding that the proposed parking supply is more
than sufficient to meet the City's criteria and could be further reduced to potentially provide additional public space
or wider marked spaces for guests and residents.

                               PUBLIC WORKS
                               MEMORANDUM


DATE:          November 12, 2013

TO:            Lee Smith, Senior Planner

FROM:          John Welch, City Engineer

SUBJECT:       Laurel Court Phases 1 and 2 Development (807-833 Laurel Avenue)

Comments regarding the plan for the proposed Laurel Court Phases 1 and 2, dated September 16,
2013, are as follow:

The engineer must submit a calculation of the existing and proposed impervious areas for this
development. Insofar as the developer is the same that developed the contiguous property to the
west, that property must be included in the impervious area calculation. Stormwater detention is
required, for both developments, if the total impervious area created by both developments
exceeds 16,000 square feet (Watershed Development Ordinance, Article IV, Section A.6).

The proposed development is tributary to the Central Avenue sanitary sewer. The engineer must
submit a calculation of the existing capacity of the Central Avenue sanitary sewer, between
Elmwood Drive and Beverly Place, in order to determine if it has sufficient capacity to serve the
proposed development, and existing load without surcharging.

The proposed plan includes a parallel parking bay on Laurel Avenue. On-street parking is
prohibited between 819 Laurel Avenue and Hickory Street. The proposed parking bay will
eliminate the existing parkway, including existing lawn and trees, and is not deemed necessary
by the Department of Public Works. The proposed parking bay will interfere with snow removal.

Section 151.008(B)(7) of the Highland Park Code requires that overhead utility lines adjacent to
the development be buried. There are two existing poles in the alley north of the development.
There is an existing pole near Hickory Street that was not required to be removed during the
construction of that development, and should be reviewed in conjunction with the adjacent
burial.

Contact me with any comments or concerns.




c:      Ramesh Kanapareddy, Director of Public Works
        William Stewart, Deputy Director of Public Works
